					<h1 id="section_0">Harley-Davidson</h1>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Harley Davidson" redirects here. For the American rugby union player, see <a href="/wiki/Harley_Davidson_(rugby_union)" title="Harley Davidson (rugby union)">Harley Davidson (rugby union)</a>. For the Iowa school district, see <a href="/wiki/Hampton-Dumont_Community_School_District" title="Hampton-Dumont Community School District">Hampton-Dumont Community School District</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Harley-Davidson, Inc.</b>, <b>H-D</b>, or <b>Harley</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle" title="Motorcycle">motorcycle</a> manufacturer founded in 1903 in <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a>. It was one of two major American motorcycle manufacturers to survive the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Indian_(motorcycle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian (motorcycle)">Indian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PopMechP2_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopMechP2-3">[3]</a></sup> The company has survived numerous ownership arrangements, subsidiary arrangements, periods of poor economic health and product quality, and intense global competition<sup id="cite_ref-hotbikeweb_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hotbikeweb-4">[4]</a></sup> to become one of the world's largest motorcycle manufacturers and an iconic brand widely known for its loyal following. There are owner clubs and events worldwide, as well as a company-sponsored, brand-focused museum.

href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Harley-Davidson&amp;params=43_02_46_N_87_57_36_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">43°02′46″N</span> <span class="longitude">87°57′36″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">43.04611°N 87.96000°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">43.04611; -87.96000</span></span></span></a></span></span></span>
</p><p>Harley-Davidson is noted for a style of customization that gave rise to the <a href="/wiki/Chopper_(motorcycle)" title="Chopper (motorcycle)">chopper</a> motorcycle style.<sup id="cite_ref-wfwvmg_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wfwvmg-5">[5]</a></sup> The company traditionally marketed heavyweight, air-cooled <a href="/wiki/Cruiser_(motorcycle)" title="Cruiser (motorcycle)">cruiser</a> motorcycles with <a href="/wiki/Engine_displacement" title="Engine displacement">engine displacements</a> greater than 700 cc, but it has broadened its offerings to include more contemporary <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_VRSC" title="Harley-Davidson VRSC">VRSC</a> (2002) and middle-weight <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Street" title="Harley-Davidson Street">Street</a> (2015) platforms.
</p><p>Harley-Davidson manufactures its motorcycles at factories in York, Pennsylvania; Milwaukee, Wisconsin; Kansas City, Missouri (closing); Manaus, Brazil; and Bawal, India. Construction of a new plant in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> began in late 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The company markets its products worldwide, and also licenses and markets merchandise under the Harley-Davidson brand, among them apparel, home decor and ornaments, accessories, toys, scale figures of its motorcycles, and video games based on its motorcycle line and the community.
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Founders_of_Harley-Davidson_The_North_Shore_Bulletin_Dec_1920.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Founders_of_Harley-Davidson_The_North_Shore_Bulletin_Dec_1920.jpg/220px-Founders_of_Harley-Davidson_The_North_Shore_Bulletin_Dec_1920.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1184" data-file-height="628"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 117px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Founders_of_Harley-Davidson_The_North_Shore_Bulletin_Dec_1920.jpg/220px-Founders_of_Harley-Davidson_The_North_Shore_Bulletin_Dec_1920.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="117" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Founders_of_Harley-Davidson_The_North_Shore_Bulletin_Dec_1920.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>From left: William A. Davidson, Walter Davidson, Sr., <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Davidson_(motorcycling)" title="Arthur Davidson (motorcycling)">Arthur Davidson</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_S._Harley" title="William S. Harley">William S. Harley</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1901, 20 year-old <a href="/wiki/William_S._Harley" title="William S. Harley">William S. Harley</a> drew up plans for a small engine with a <a href="/wiki/Engine_displacement" title="Engine displacement">displacement</a> of 7.07 cubic inches (116 cc) and four-inch (102 mm) <a href="/wiki/Flywheel" title="Flywheel">flywheels</a><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> designed for use in a regular pedal-bicycle frame. Over the next two years, he and his childhood friend <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Davidson_(Harley-Davidson_founder)" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur Davidson (Harley-Davidson founder)">Arthur Davidson</a> worked on their <a href="/wiki/Motorized_bicycle" title="Motorized bicycle">motor-bicycle</a> using the northside <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a> machine shop at the home of their friend Henry Melk. It was finished in 1903 with the help of Arthur's brother Walter Davidson. Upon testing their power-cycle, Harley and the Davidson brothers found it unable to climb the hills around Milwaukee without pedal assistance, and they wrote off their first motor-bicycle as a valuable learning experiment.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p><p>The three began work on a new and improved machine with an engine of 24.74 cubic inches (405 cc) with 9.75 in (24.8 cm) flywheels weighing 28 lb (13 kg). Its advanced loop-frame pattern was similar to the 1903 Milwaukee Merkel motorcycle designed by Joseph Merkel, later of <a href="/wiki/Flying_Merkel" title="Flying Merkel">Flying Merkel</a> fame. The bigger engine and loop-frame design took it out of the motorized bicycle category and marked the path to future motorcycle designs. They also received help with their bigger engine from outboard motor pioneer <a href="/wiki/Ole_Evinrude" title="Ole Evinrude">Ole Evinrude</a>, who was then building gas engines of his own design for automotive use on Milwaukee's Lake Street.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_Monocylinder.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Harley-Davidson_Monocylinder.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_Monocylinder.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="965" data-file-height="708"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 161px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Harley-Davidson_Monocylinder.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_Monocylinder.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="161" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_Monocylinder.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prototype</div></div></div>
<p>The prototype of the new loop-frame Harley-Davidson was assembled in a 10 ft × 15 ft (3.0 m × 4.6 m) shed in the Davidson family backyard.<sup id="cite_ref-Wagner,_2003._pp.45–62_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wagner,_2003._pp.45%E2%80%9362-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Most of the major parts, however, were made elsewhere, including some probably fabricated at the West Milwaukee railshops where oldest brother William A. Davidson was toolroom foreman. This prototype machine was functional by September 8, 1904, when it competed in a Milwaukee motorcycle race held at State Fair Park. Edward Hildebrand rode it and placed fourth in the race.<sup id="cite_ref-Wagner,_2003._pp.45–62_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wagner,_2003._pp.45%E2%80%9362-10">[10]</a></sup></p><p>In January 1905, the company placed small advertisements in the <i>Automobile and Cycle Trade Journal</i> offering bare Harley-Davidson engines to the do-it-yourself trade. By April, they were producing complete motorcycles on a very limited basis. That year, Harley-Davidson dealer Carl H. Lang of Chicago sold three bikes from the five built in the Davidson backyard shed. Years later, the company moved the original shed to the Juneau Avenue factory where it stood for many decades as a tribute.
</p><p>In 1906, Harley and the Davidson brothers built their first factory on Chestnut Street (later Juneau Avenue),<sup id="cite_ref-H-Dtimeline1900s_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H-Dtimeline1900s-12">[12]</a></sup> at the current location of Harley-Davidson's corporate headquarters. The first Juneau Avenue plant was a 40 ft × 60 ft (12 m × 18 m) single-story wooden structure. The company produced about 50 motorcycles that year.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1907_Harley_Davidson.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/1907_Harley_Davidson.jpg/220px-1907_Harley_Davidson.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="411" data-file-height="233"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 125px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/1907_Harley_Davidson.jpg/220px-1907_Harley_Davidson.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="125" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1907_Harley_Davidson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1907 model.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1916.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1916.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1916.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="437"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 120px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1916.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1916.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="120" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1916.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harley-Davidson 1,000 cc HT 1916</div></div></div>
<p>In 1907, William S. Harley graduated from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison" title="University of Wisconsin–Madison">University of Wisconsin–Madison</a> with a degree in mechanical engineering. That year, they expanded the factory with a second floor and later with facings and additions of Milwaukee pale yellow ("cream") brick. With the new facilities, production increased to 150 motorcycles in 1907. The company was officially incorporated that September. They also began selling their motorcycles to police departments around this time, a market that has been important to them ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In 1907, William A. Davidson quit his job as tool foreman for the Milwaukee Road railroad and joined the Motor Company.
</p><p>Production in 1905 and 1906 were all single-cylinder models with 26.84 cubic inch (440 cc) engines. In February 1907, they displayed a prototype model at the Chicago Automobile Show with a 45-degree <a href="/wiki/V-Twin" class="mw-redirect" title="V-Twin">V-Twin</a> engine. Very few V-Twin models were built between 1907 and 1910. These first V-Twins displaced 53.68 cubic inches (880 cc) and produced about 7 horsepower (5.2 kW). This gave about double the power of the first singles, and top speed was about 60 mph (100 km/h). Production jumped from 450 motorcycles in 1908 to 1,149 machines in 1909.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_Davidson_Motor_Company_The_Implement_Age_v16.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Harley_Davidson_Motor_Company_The_Implement_Age_v16.jpg/220px-Harley_Davidson_Motor_Company_The_Implement_Age_v16.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="99" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="819" data-file-height="369"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 99px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Harley_Davidson_Motor_Company_The_Implement_Age_v16.jpg/220px-Harley_Davidson_Motor_Company_The_Implement_Age_v16.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="99" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_Davidson_Motor_Company_The_Implement_Age_v16.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harley-Davidson works in 1911</div></div></div>
<p>In 1911, the company introduced an improved V-Twin model with a displacement of 49.48 cubic inches (811 cc) and mechanically operated intake valves, as opposed to the "automatic" intake valves used on earlier V-Twins that opened by engine vacuum. It was smaller than earlier twins but gave better performance. After 1913, the majority of bikes produced by Harley-Davidson were V-Twin models.
</p><p>In 1912, Harley-Davidson introduced their patented "Ful-Floteing Seat" which was suspended by a coil spring inside the seat tube.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The spring tension could be adjusted to suit the rider's weight, and more than 3 inches (76 mm) of travel was available.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Harley-Davidson used seats of this type until 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>By 1913, the yellow brick factory had been demolished and a new five-story structure had been built on the site which took up two blocks along Juneau Avenue and around the corner on 38th Street. Despite the competition, Harley-Davidson was already pulling ahead of <a href="/wiki/Indian_(motorcycle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian (motorcycle)">Indian</a> and dominated motorcycle racing after 1914. Production that year swelled to 16,284 machines.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RalphHepburn1922.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/RalphHepburn1922.jpg/170px-RalphHepburn1922.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="216" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="549"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 216px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/RalphHepburn1922.jpg/170px-RalphHepburn1922.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="216" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RalphHepburn1922.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ralph_Hepburn" title="Ralph Hepburn">Ralph Hepburn</a> on his Harley racing bike in 1919</div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: World War I" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1917, the United States entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and the military demanded motorcycles for the war effort.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Harleys had already been used by the military in the <a href="/wiki/Pancho_Villa_Expedition" title="Pancho Villa Expedition">Pancho Villa Expedition</a><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> but World War I was the first time that it was adopted for military issue, first with the British <a href="/wiki/Model_H" class="mw-redirect" title="Model H">Model H</a> produced by <a href="/wiki/Triumph_Motorcycles_Ltd" title="Triumph Motorcycles Ltd">Triumph Motorcycles Ltd</a> in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The U.S. military purchased over 20,000 motorcycles from Harley-Davidson.<sup id="cite_ref-PBS_HD_9_2006_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBS_HD_9_2006-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycles">Bicycles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Bicycles" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Harley-Davidson launched a line of bicycles in 1917 in hopes of recruiting customers for its motorcycles. Models included the traditional diamond frame men's bicycle, a <a href="/wiki/Step-through_frame" title="Step-through frame">step-through frame</a> 3–18 "Ladies Standard", and a 5–17 "Boy Scout" for youth. The effort was discontinued in 1923 because of disappointing sales.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The bicycles were built for Harley-Davidson in Dayton, Ohio by the Davis Machine Company from 1917 to 1921, when Davis stopped manufacturing bicycles.<sup id="cite_ref-HeroBicycle_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HeroBicycle-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1920s">1920s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1920s" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1923.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1923.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1923.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="485"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 133px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1923.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1923.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="133" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_1000_cc_HT_1923.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harley-Davidson 1000 cc HT 1923</div></div></div>
<p>By 1920, Harley-Davidson was the largest motorcycle manufacturer in the world, with 28,189 machines produced and dealers in 67 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-H-Dtimeline_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H-Dtimeline-25">[25]</a></sup> In 1921, Otto Walker set a record on a Harley-Davidson as the first motorcycle to win a race at an average speed greater than 100 mph (160 km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>Harley-Davidson put several improvements in place during the 1920s, such as a new 74 cubic inch (1,212.6  cc) V-Twin introduced in 1921, and the "teardrop" gas tank in 1925. They added a front brake in 1928, although only on the J/JD models.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In the late summer of 1929, Harley-Davidson introduced its 45 cubic inch (737 cc) flathead V-Twin to compete with the <a href="/wiki/Indian_101_Scout" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian 101 Scout">Indian 101 Scout</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Excelsior_Super_X" title="Excelsior Super X">Excelsior Super X</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle68_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle68-29">[29]</a></sup> This was the "D" model produced from 1929 to 1931.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Riders of Indian motorcycles derisively referred to it as the "three cylinder Harley" because the generator was upright and parallel to the front cylinder.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Depression">Great Depression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Great Depression" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_1200_cc_SV_1931.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Harley-Davidson_1200_cc_SV_1931.jpg/200px-Harley-Davidson_1200_cc_SV_1931.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="172" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="688"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 172px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Harley-Davidson_1200_cc_SV_1931.jpg/200px-Harley-Davidson_1200_cc_SV_1931.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="172" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_1200_cc_SV_1931.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harley-Davidson 1,200 cc SV 1931</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> began a few months after the introduction of their 45 cu in (740 cm<sup>3</sup>) model. Harley-Davidson's sales fell from 21,000 in 1929 to 3,703 in 1933. Despite this, Harley-Davidson unveiled a new lineup for 1934, which included a flathead engine and <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> styling.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p><p>In order to survive the remainder of the Depression, the company manufactured industrial powerplants based on their motorcycle engines. They also designed and built a three-wheeled delivery vehicle called the <a href="/wiki/Servi-Car" class="mw-redirect" title="Servi-Car">Servi-Car</a>, which remained in production until 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle68_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle68-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vintage_harley_davidson_photo_in_madrid_spain_2011.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Vintage_harley_davidson_photo_in_madrid_spain_2011.jpg/220px-Vintage_harley_davidson_photo_in_madrid_spain_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Vintage_harley_davidson_photo_in_madrid_spain_2011.jpg/220px-Vintage_harley_davidson_photo_in_madrid_spain_2011.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vintage_harley_davidson_photo_in_madrid_spain_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harley-Davidson UL</div></div></div>
<p>In the mid-1930s, Alfred Rich Child opened a production line in Japan with the 74 cu in (1,210 cm<sup>3</sup>) VL. The Japanese license-holder, Sankyo Seiyaku Corporation, severed its business relations with Harley-Davidson in 1936 and continued manufacturing the VL under the <a href="/wiki/Rikuo_Motorcycle" title="Rikuo Motorcycle">Rikuo</a> name.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_Sales_Co.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Harley-Davidson_Sales_Co.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_Sales_Co.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="960"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 141px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Harley-Davidson_Sales_Co.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_Sales_Co.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="141" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_Sales_Co.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harley-Davidson dealer in Texas, ca. 1930–1945</div></div></div>
<p>An 80 cubic inches (1,300 cm<sup>3</sup>) flathead engine was added to the line in 1935, by which time the single-cylinder motorcycles had been discontinued.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle92_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle92-34">[34]</a></sup></p><p>In 1936, the 61E and 61EL models with the "<a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Knucklehead_engine" title="Harley-Davidson Knucklehead engine">Knucklehead</a>" <a href="/wiki/Overhead_valve" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhead valve">OHV</a> engines were introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle94_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle94-35">[35]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Valvetrain" title="Valvetrain">Valvetrain</a> problems in early Knucklehead engines required a redesign halfway through its first year of production and retrofitting of the new valvetrain on earlier engines.<sup id="cite_ref-ClassicMotorcycles53_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ClassicMotorcycles53-36">[36]</a></sup></p><p>By 1937, all Harley-Davidson flathead engines were equipped with dry-sump oil recirculation systems similar to the one introduced in the "Knucklehead" OHV engine. The revised 74 cubic inches (1,210 cm<sup>3</sup>) V and VL models were renamed U and UL, the 80 cu in (1,300 cm<sup>3</sup>) VH and VLH to be renamed UH and ULH, and the 45 cu in (740 cm<sup>3</sup>) R to be renamed W.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle94_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle94-35">[35]</a></sup></p><p>In 1941, the 74 cubic-inch "Knucklehead" was introduced as the F and the <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_FL" title="Harley-Davidson FL">FL</a>. The 80 cu in (1,300 cm<sup>3</sup>) flathead UH and ULH models were discontinued after 1941, while the 74 cubic inch U &amp; UL flathead models were produced up to 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle94_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle94-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: World War II" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Xa-600.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Xa-600.jpg/220px-Xa-600.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="506"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 186px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Xa-600.jpg/220px-Xa-600.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="186" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Xa-600.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harley copied the <a href="/wiki/BMW_motorcycles" class="mw-redirect" title="BMW motorcycles">BMW</a> R71 to produce its <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_XA" title="Harley-Davidson XA">XA model</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>One of only two American cycle manufacturers to survive the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-PopMechP2_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopMechP2-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UltiMoto17_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UltiMoto17-37">[37]</a></sup> Harley-Davidson again produced large numbers of motorcycles for the US Army in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and resumed civilian production afterwards, producing a range of large V-twin motorcycles that were successful both on racetracks and for private buyers.
</p><p>Harley-Davidson, on the eve of World War II, was already supplying the Army with a military-specific version of its 45 cubic inches (740 cm<sup>3</sup>) WL line, called the <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_WLA" title="Harley-Davidson WLA">WLA</a>. The A in this case stood for "Army". Upon the outbreak of war, the company, along with most other manufacturing enterprises, shifted to war work. More than 90,000 military motorcycles, mostly WLAs and WLCs (the Canadian version) were produced, many to be provided to allies.<sup id="cite_ref-wildthing_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wildthing-38">[38]</a></sup> Harley-Davidson received two <a href="/w/index.php?title=Army-Navy_%27E%27_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Army-Navy 'E' Award (page does not exist)">Army-Navy 'E' Awards</a>, one in 1943 and the other in 1945, which were awarded for Excellence in Production.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HD_Liberator.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/HD_Liberator.jpg/220px-HD_Liberator.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/HD_Liberator.jpg/220px-HD_Liberator.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HD_Liberator.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harley-Davidson produced the WLC for the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_military" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian military">Canadian military</a></div></div></div>
<p>Shipments to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Lend-Lease" title="Lend-Lease">Lend-Lease</a> program numbered at least 30,000.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The WLAs produced during all four years of war production generally have 1942 serial numbers. Production of the WLA stopped at the end of World War II, but was resumed from 1950 to 1952 for use in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>.
</p><p>The U.S. Army also asked Harley-Davidson to produce a new motorcycle with many of the features of <a href="/wiki/History_of_BMW_motorcycles" title="History of BMW motorcycles">BMW's</a> side-valve and <a href="/wiki/Drive_shaft" title="Drive shaft">shaft-driven</a> R71. Harley-Davidson largely copied the BMW engine and drive train and produced the shaft-driven 750 cc 1942 <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_XA" title="Harley-Davidson XA">Harley-Davidson XA</a>. This shared no dimensions, no parts or no design concepts (except side valves) with any prior Harley-Davidson engine. Due to the superior cooling of the <a href="/wiki/Flat-twin" class="mw-redirect" title="Flat-twin">flat-twin</a> engine with the cylinders across the frame, Harley's XA cylinder heads ran 100 °F (56 °C) cooler than its V-twins.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The XA never entered full production: the motorcycle by that time had been eclipsed by the <a href="/wiki/Jeep" title="Jeep">Jeep</a> as the Army's general purpose vehicle, and the WLA—already in production—was sufficient for its limited police, escort, and courier roles. Only 1,000 were made and the XA never went into full production. It remains the only shaft-driven Harley-Davidson ever made.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Small_Harleys:_Hummers_and_Aermacchis">Small Harleys: Hummers and Aermacchis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Small Harleys: Hummers and Aermacchis" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_Hummer.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Harley-Davidson_Hummer.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_Hummer.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Harley-Davidson_Hummer.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_Hummer.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_Hummer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Hummer" title="Harley-Davidson Hummer">Harley-Davidson Hummer</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Hummer" title="Harley-Davidson Hummer">Harley-Davidson Hummer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Topper" title="Harley-Davidson Topper">Harley-Davidson Topper</a></div>
<p>As part of <a href="/wiki/War_reparations" title="War reparations">war reparations</a>, Harley-Davidson acquired the design of a small German motorcycle, the <a href="/wiki/DKW_RT_125" title="DKW RT 125">DKW RT 125</a>, which they adapted, manufactured, and sold from 1948 to 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-HummerClub_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HummerClub-41">[41]</a></sup> Various models were made, including the <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Hummer" title="Harley-Davidson Hummer">Hummer</a> from 1955 to 1959, but they are all colloquially referred to as "Hummers" at present.<sup id="cite_ref-HummerDotCom_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HummerDotCom-42">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Small_Arms_Company" title="Birmingham Small Arms Company">BSA</a> in the United Kingdom took the same design as the foundation of their <a href="/wiki/BSA_Bantam" title="BSA Bantam">BSA Bantam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EncycMoto37_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EncycMoto37-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aermacchi_Turismo_Veloce_1971_crop.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Aermacchi_Turismo_Veloce_1971_crop.jpg/220px-Aermacchi_Turismo_Veloce_1971_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="618" data-file-height="344"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 122px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Aermacchi_Turismo_Veloce_1971_crop.jpg/220px-Aermacchi_Turismo_Veloce_1971_crop.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="122" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aermacchi_Turismo_Veloce_1971_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1971 Aermacchi Harley-Davidson Turismo Veloce</div></div></div>
<p>In 1960, Harley-Davidson consolidated the Model 165 and Hummer lines into the Super-10, introduced the Topper scooter,<sup id="cite_ref-EncycMoto252_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EncycMoto252-44">[44]</a></sup> and bought fifty percent of <a href="/wiki/Aermacchi" title="Aermacchi">Aermacchi</a>'s motorcycle division.<sup id="cite_ref-EncycMoto252_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EncycMoto252-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MotoClassicsSprint350_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MotoClassicsSprint350-45">[45]</a></sup> Importation of <a href="/wiki/Aermacchi" title="Aermacchi">Aermacchi</a>'s 250 cc horizontal single began the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-MotoClassicsSprint350_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MotoClassicsSprint350-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EncycMoto74_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EncycMoto74-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle187_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle187-47">[47]</a></sup> The bike bore Harley-Davidson badges and was marketed as the Harley-Davidson Sprint.<sup id="cite_ref-EncycMoto74_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EncycMoto74-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle187_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle187-47">[47]</a></sup> The engine of the Sprint was increased to 350 cc in 1969<sup id="cite_ref-MotoClassicsSprint350_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MotoClassicsSprint350-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle215_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle215-48">[48]</a></sup> and would remain that size until 1974, when the four-stroke Sprint was discontinued.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle215_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle215-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>After the Pacer and Scat models were discontinued at the end of 1965, the Bobcat became the last of Harley-Davidson's American-made <a href="/wiki/Two-stroke_engine" title="Two-stroke engine">two-stroke</a> motorcycles. The Bobcat was manufactured only in the 1966 model year.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle193_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle193-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>Harley-Davidson replaced their American-made lightweight two-stroke motorcycles with the Italian <a href="/wiki/Aermacchi" title="Aermacchi">Aermacchi</a>-built two-stroke powered M-65, M-65S, and Rapido. The M-65 had a semi-step-through frame and tank. The M-65S was a M-65 with a larger tank that eliminated the step-through feature. The Rapido was a larger bike with a 125 cc engine.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle218_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle218-50">[50]</a></sup> The Aermacchi-built Harley-Davidsons became entirely two-stroke powered when the 250 cc two-stroke SS-250 replaced the four-stroke 350 cc Sprint in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-Chronicle247_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle247-51">[51]</a></sup></p><p>Harley-Davidson purchased full control of <a href="/wiki/Aermacchi" title="Aermacchi">Aermacchi</a>'s motorcycle production in 1974 and continued making two-stroke motorcycles there until 1978, when they sold the facility to <a href="/wiki/Cagiva" title="Cagiva">Cagiva</a>, owned by the Castiglioni family.<sup id="cite_ref-EncycMoto252_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EncycMoto252-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Overseas">Overseas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Overseas" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Established in 1918, the oldest continuously operating Harley-Davidson dealership outside of the United States is in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-employees_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-employees-52">[52]</a></sup> Sales in Japan started in 1912<sup id="cite_ref-employees_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-employees-52">[52]</a></sup> then in 1929, Harley-Davidsons were produced in Japan under license to the company <a href="/wiki/Rikuo_Motorcycle" title="Rikuo Motorcycle">Rikuo</a> (Rikuo Internal Combustion Company)<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> under the name of Harley-Davidson and using the company's tooling, and later under the name Rikuo. Production continued until 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-Vanneck_1998_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneck_1998-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sucher_1981_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sucher_1981-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Tarnished_reputation">Tarnished reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tarnished reputation" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ZweiRadMuseumNSU_EasyRider.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/ZweiRadMuseumNSU_EasyRider.JPG/170px-ZweiRadMuseumNSU_EasyRider.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1493" data-file-height="2100"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 239px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/ZweiRadMuseumNSU_EasyRider.JPG/170px-ZweiRadMuseumNSU_EasyRider.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="239" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ZweiRadMuseumNSU_EasyRider.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Replica of the "<a href="/wiki/Captain_America_(motorcycle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain America (motorcycle)">Captain America bike</a>" from the film <i><a href="/wiki/Easy_Rider" title="Easy Rider">Easy Rider</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>In 1952, following their application to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_International_Trade_Commission" title="United States International Trade Commission">U.S. Tariff Commission</a> for a 40 percent tax on imported motorcycles, Harley-Davidson was charged with restrictive practices.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_6.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Harley-Davidson_6.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_6.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Harley-Davidson_6.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_6.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_6.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>AMF H-D Electra Glide</div></div></div>
<p>In 1969, <a href="/wiki/American_Machine_and_Foundry" title="American Machine and Foundry">American Machine and Foundry</a> (AMF) bought the company,<sup id="cite_ref-amfacq_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amfacq-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fftbuy_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fftbuy-58">[58]</a></sup> streamlined production, and slashed the workforce. This tactic resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">labor strike</a> and lower-quality bikes.<sup id="cite_ref-hotbikeweb_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hotbikeweb-4">[4]</a></sup> The bikes were expensive and inferior in performance, handling, and quality to Japanese motorcycles. Sales and quality declined, and the company almost went bankrupt.<sup id="cite_ref-hotbikeweb_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hotbikeweb-4">[4]</a></sup> The "Harley-Davidson" name was mocked as "Hardly Ableson", "Hardly Driveable," and "Hogly Ferguson",<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
and the nickname "Hog" became <a href="/wiki/Pejorative" title="Pejorative">pejorative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p><p>In 1977, following the successful manufacture of the Liberty Edition to commemorate America's <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bicentennial" title="United States Bicentennial">bicentennial</a> in 1976,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Harley-Davidson produced what has become one of its most controversial models, the <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Confederate_Edition" title="Harley-Davidson Confederate Edition">Harley-Davidson Confederate Edition</a>. The bike was essentially a stock Harley-Davidson with <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate</a>-specific paint and details.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Restructuring_and_revival">Restructuring and revival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Restructuring and revival" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1981, AMF sold the company to a group of 13 investors led by <a href="/wiki/Vaughn_Beals" title="Vaughn Beals">Vaughn Beals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willie_G._Davidson" title="Willie G. Davidson">Willie G. Davidson</a> for $80 million.<sup id="cite_ref-wild_thing_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wild_thing-64">[64]</a></sup> Inventory was strictly controlled using the <a href="/wiki/Just-in-time_(business)" class="mw-redirect" title="Just-in-time (business)">just-in-time</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p><p>In the early eighties, Harley-Davidson claimed that Japanese manufacturers were importing motorcycles into the US in such volume as to harm or threaten to harm domestic producers.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> After an investigation by the U.S. International Trade Commission, President Reagan in 1983 imposed a 45 percent tariff on imported bikes with engine capacities greater than 700 cc. Harley-Davidson subsequently rejected offers of assistance from Japanese motorcycle makers.<sup id="cite_ref-7/83_US_IMPOSES_45%_TARIFF_ON_IMPORTED_MOTORCYCLES_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7/83_US_IMPOSES_45%_TARIFF_ON_IMPORTED_MOTORCYCLES-67">[67]</a></sup> However, the company did offer to drop the request for the tariff in exchange for loan guarantees from the Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-HDCentury_HarleyVJapanMyth_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDCentury_HarleyVJapanMyth-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p><p>Rather than trying to match the Japanese, the new management deliberately exploited the "retro" appeal of the machines, building motorcycles that deliberately adopted the look and feel of their earlier machines and the subsequent customizations of owners of that era. Many components such as brakes, forks, shocks, carburetors, electrics and wheels were outsourced from foreign manufacturers and quality increased, technical improvements were made, and buyers slowly returned.
</p><p>Harley-Davidson bought the "Sub Shock" cantilever-swingarm rear suspension design from Missouri engineer Bill Davis and developed it into its <a href="/wiki/Softail" title="Softail">Softail</a> series of motorcycles, introduced in 1984 with the FXST Softail.<sup id="cite_ref-HDCentury_FatherSoftail_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDCentury_FatherSoftail-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>In response to possible motorcycle market loss due to the aging of baby-boomers, Harley-Davidson bought luxury <a href="/wiki/Motorhome" title="Motorhome">motorhome</a> manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Holiday_Rambler" title="Holiday Rambler">Holiday Rambler</a> in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In 1996, the company sold Holiday Rambler to the <a href="/wiki/Monaco_Coach_Corporation" title="Monaco Coach Corporation">Monaco Coach Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p><p>The "Sturgis" model, boasting a dual belt-drive, was introduced initially in 1980 and was made for three years. This bike was then brought back as a commemorative model in 1991.
By 1990, with the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Fat_Boy" title="Harley-Davidson Fat Boy">"Fat Boy"</a>, Harley-Davidson once again became the sales leader in the heavyweight (over 750 cc) market.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> At the time of the Fat Boy model introduction, a story rapidly spread that its silver paint job and other features were inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_B-29_Superfortress" title="Boeing B-29 Superfortress">B-29</a>; and Fat Boy was a combination of the names of the atomic bombs <a href="/wiki/Fat_Man" title="Fat Man">Fat Man</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Boy" title="Little Boy">Little Boy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HDCentury_FatBoy_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDCentury_FatBoy-74">[74]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Snopes" title="Snopes">Urban Legend Reference Pages</a> lists this story as an <a href="/wiki/Urban_legend" title="Urban legend">urban legend</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p><p>1993 and 1994 saw the replacement of FXR models with the Dyna (FXD), which became the sole rubber mount FX Big Twin frame in 1994. The FXR was revived briefly from 1999 to 2000 for special limited editions (FXR<sup>2</sup>, FXR<sup>3</sup> &amp; FXR<sup>4</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-HDCentury_EndOfFXR_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDCentury_EndOfFXR-77">[77]</a></sup></p><p>Construction started on the $75 million, 130,000 square-foot (12,000 m<sup>2</sup>) <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Museum" title="Harley-Davidson Museum">Harley-Davidson Museum</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Menomonee_Valley" title="Menomonee Valley">Menomonee Valley</a> on June 1, 2006. It opened in 2008 and houses the company's vast collection of historic motorcycles and corporate archives, along with a restaurant, café and meeting space.<sup id="cite_ref-museum_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-museum-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Buell_Motorcycle_Company">Buell Motorcycle Company</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Buell Motorcycle Company" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Buell_Motorcycle_Company" title="Buell Motorcycle Company">Buell Motorcycle Company</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Buell_XB9SX_a.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Buell_XB9SX_a.jpg/220px-Buell_XB9SX_a.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Buell_XB9SX_a.jpg/220px-Buell_XB9SX_a.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Buell_XB9SX_a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Buell Lightning XB9SX</div></div></div>
<p>Harley-Davidson's association with <a href="/wiki/Sport_bike" title="Sport bike">sportbike</a> manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Buell_Motorcycle_Company" title="Buell Motorcycle Company">Buell Motorcycle Company</a> began in 1987 when they supplied Buell with fifty surplus XR1000 engines. Buell continued to buy engines from Harley-Davidson until 1993, when Harley-Davidson bought 49 percent of the Buell Motorcycle Company.<sup id="cite_ref-MCJuly08_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCJuly08-79">[79]</a></sup> Harley-Davidson increased its share in Buell to ninety-eight percent in 1998, and to complete ownership in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p><p>In an attempt to attract newcomers to motorcycling in general and to Harley-Davidson in particular, Buell developed a low-cost, low-maintenance motorcycle. The resulting single-cylinder <a href="/wiki/Buell_Blast" title="Buell Blast">Buell Blast</a> was introduced in 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-MOBlast_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOBlast-81">[81]</a></sup> and was made through 2009, which, according to Buell, was to be the final year of production.<sup id="cite_ref-Procter2009_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Procter2009-82">[82]</a></sup> The Buell Blast was the training vehicle for the Harley-Davidson Rider's Edge New Rider Course from 2000 until May 2014, when the company re-branded the training academy and started using the <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Street" title="Harley-Davidson Street">Harley-Davidson Street 500</a> motorcycles. In those 14 years, more than 350,000 participants in the course learned to ride on the Buell Blast.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p><p>On October 15, 2009, Harley-Davidson Inc. issued an official statement that it would be discontinuing the Buell line and ceasing production immediately.<sup id="cite_ref-Harley-Davidson.com_Oct_15_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harley-Davidson.com_Oct_15-84">[84]</a></sup> The stated reason was to focus on the Harley-Davidson brand. The company refused to consider selling Buell.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Founder <a href="/wiki/Erik_Buell" title="Erik Buell">Erik Buell</a> subsequently established <a href="/wiki/Erik_Buell_Racing" title="Erik Buell Racing">Erik Buell Racing</a> and continued to manufacture and develop the company's <a href="/wiki/Buell_1125R" title="Buell 1125R">1125RR</a> racing motorcycle.<sup id="cite_ref-MotoUSA1190RR1stLook_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MotoUSA1190RR1stLook-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="First_overseas_factory_in_Brazil">First overseas factory in Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: First overseas factory in Brazil" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1998 the first Harley-Davidson factory outside the US opened in <a href="/wiki/Manaus,_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Manaus, Brazil">Manaus, Brazil</a>, taking advantage of the <a href="/wiki/Free_Economic_Zone_of_Manaus" title="Free Economic Zone of Manaus">free economic zone</a> there. The location was positioned to sell motorcycles in the southern hemisphere market.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="100th_anniversary">100th anniversary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 100th anniversary" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Harley-Davidson hired <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> to headline their 100th anniversary event on September 1, 2003. Other performers included <a href="/wiki/The_Doobie_Brothers" title="The Doobie Brothers">The Doobie Brothers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kid_Rock" title="Kid Rock">Kid Rock</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tim_McGraw" title="Tim McGraw">Tim McGraw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Claims_of_stock_price_manipulation">Claims of stock price manipulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Claims of stock price manipulation" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HOG_5years.PNG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/39/HOG_5years.PNG" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="200"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 300px;height: 200px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/39/HOG_5years.PNG" data-alt="" data-width="300" data-height="200" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption">Harley-Davidson Inc (NYSE:HOG) stock price (source: ZenoBank.com)</div></div></div>
<p>During its period of peak demand, during the late 1990s and early first decade of the 21st century, Harley-Davidson embarked on a program of expanding the number of dealerships throughout the country. At the same time, its current dealers typically had waiting lists that extended up to a year for some of the most popular models. Harley-Davidson, like the auto manufacturers, records a sale not when a consumer buys their product, but rather when it is delivered to a dealer. Therefore, it is possible for the manufacturer to inflate sales numbers by requiring dealers to accept more inventory than desired in a practice called <a href="/wiki/Channel_stuffing" title="Channel stuffing">channel stuffing</a>. When demand softened following the unique 2003 model year, this news led to a dramatic decline in the stock price. In April 2004 alone, the price of HOG shares dropped from more than $60 to less than $40. Immediately prior to this decline, retiring CEO Jeffrey Bleustein profited $42 million on the exercise of <a href="/wiki/Employee_stock_option" title="Employee stock option">employee stock options</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Harley-Davidson was named as a defendant in numerous <a href="/wiki/Class_action" title="Class action">class action</a> suits filed by investors who claimed they were intentionally defrauded by Harley-Davidson's management and directors.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> By January 2007, the price of Harley-Davidson shares reached $70.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Problems_with_Police_Touring_models">Problems with Police Touring models</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Problems with Police Touring models" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Starting around 2000, several police departments started reporting problems with high speed instability on the Harley-Davidson Touring motorcycles.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>  A <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh, North Carolina</a> police officer, Charles Paul, was killed when his 2002 police touring motorcycle crashed after reportedly experiencing a high <a href="/wiki/Speed_wobble" title="Speed wobble">speed wobble</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/California_Highway_Patrol" title="California Highway Patrol">California Highway Patrol</a> conducted testing of the Police Touring motorcycles in 2006.  The CHP test riders reported experiencing wobble or weave instability while operating the motorcycles on the test track.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_strike">2007 strike</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2007 strike" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On February 2, 2007, upon the expiration of their union contract, about 2,700 employees at Harley-Davidson Inc.'s largest manufacturing plant in <a href="/wiki/York,_Pennsylvania" title="York, Pennsylvania">York, Pennsylvania</a>, went on strike after failing to agree on wages and health benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> During the pendency of the strike, the company refused to pay for any portion of the striking employees' health care.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p><p>The day before the strike, after the union voted against the proposed contract and to authorize the strike, the company shut down all production at the plant. The York facility employs more than 3,200 workers, both union and non-union.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p><p>Harley-Davidson announced on February 16, 2007, that it had reached a labor agreement with union workers at its largest manufacturing plant, a breakthrough in the two-week-old strike.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The strike disrupted Harley-Davidson's national production and was felt in Wisconsin, where 440 employees were laid off, and many Harley suppliers also laid off workers because of the strike.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="MV_Agusta_Group">MV Agusta Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: MV Agusta Group" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On July 11, 2008, Harley-Davidson announced they had signed a definitive agreement to acquire the <a href="/wiki/MV_Agusta" title="MV Agusta">MV Agusta Group</a> for US$109 million (€70M). MV Agusta Group contains two lines of motorcycles: the high-performance <a href="/wiki/MV_Agusta" title="MV Agusta">MV Agusta</a> brand and the lightweight <a href="/wiki/Cagiva" title="Cagiva">Cagiva</a> brand.<sup id="cite_ref-SuperbikePlanet.com_July_11_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuperbikePlanet.com_July_11-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Harley-Davidson.com_July_11_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harley-Davidson.com_July_11-102">[102]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed on August 8.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p><p>On October 15, 2009, Harley-Davidson announced that it would divest its interest in MV Agusta.<sup id="cite_ref-Harley-Davidson.com_Oct_15_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harley-Davidson.com_Oct_15-84">[84]</a></sup>  Harley-Davidson Inc. sold Italian motorcycle maker MV Agusta to Claudio Castiglioni – a member of the family that had purchased Aermacchi from H-D in 1978 – for a reported 3 euros, ending the transaction in the first week of August 2010. Castiglioni was MV Agusta's former owner, and had been MV Agusta's chairman since Harley-Davidson bought it in 2008.  As part of the deal, Harley-Davidson put $26M into MV Agusta's accounts, essentially giving Castiglioni $26M to take the brand.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HarleySellsMVAgusta_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HarleySellsMVAgusta-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations_in_India">Operations in India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Operations in India" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_India" title="Harley-Davidson India">Harley-Davidson India</a></div>
<p>In August 2009, Harley-Davidson announced plans to enter the market in India and started selling motorcycles there in 2010.  The company established a subsidiary, Harley-Davidson India, in <a href="/wiki/Gurgaon" title="Gurgaon">Gurgaon</a>, near Delhi, in 2011 and created an Indian dealer network.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_crisis">Financial crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Financial crisis" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Interbrand" title="Interbrand">Interbrand</a>, the value of the Harley-Davidson brand fell by 43 percent to $4.34 billion in 2009. The fall in value is believed to be connected to the 66 percent drop in the company profits in two-quarters of the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> On April 29, 2010, Harley-Davidson stated that they must cut $54 million in manufacturing costs from its production facilities in Wisconsin, and that they would explore alternative U.S. sites to accomplish this. The announcement came in the wake of a massive company-wide restructuring, which began in early 2009 and involved the closing of two factories, one distribution center, and the planned elimination of nearly 25 percent of its total workforce (around 3,500 employees). The company announced on September 14, 2010, that it would remain in Wisconsin.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorcycle_engines">Motorcycle engines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Motorcycle engines" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_Davidson.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Harley_Davidson.jpg/170px-Harley_Davidson.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 256px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Harley_Davidson.jpg/170px-Harley_Davidson.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="256" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_Davidson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template:Ccvt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Template:Ccvt (page does not exist)">Template:Ccvt</a> V-twin</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_engine_timeline" title="Harley-Davidson engine timeline">Harley-Davidson engine timeline</a></div>
<p>The classic Harley-Davidson engines are <a href="/wiki/V-twin_engine" title="V-twin engine">V-twin engines</a>, with a 45° angle between the cylinders. The <a href="/wiki/Crankshaft" title="Crankshaft">crankshaft</a> has a single pin, and both <a href="/wiki/Piston" title="Piston">pistons</a> are connected to this pin through their <a href="/wiki/Connecting_rod" title="Connecting rod">connecting rods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wfwvmg_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wfwvmg-5">[5]</a></sup></p><p>This 45° angle is covered under several <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States patents</a> and is an engineering tradeoff that allows a large, high-torque engine in a relatively small space. It causes the cylinders to fire at uneven intervals and produces the choppy "potato-potato" sound so strongly linked to the Harley-Davidson brand.
</p><p>To simplify the engine and reduce costs, the V-twin ignition was designed to operate with a single set of points and no distributor. This is known as a dual fire ignition system, causing both spark plugs to fire regardless of which cylinder was on its compression stroke, with the other spark plug firing on its cylinder's exhaust stroke, effectively "<a href="/wiki/Wasted_spark" title="Wasted spark">wasting a spark</a>". The exhaust note is basically a throaty growling sound with some popping.
The 45° design of the engine thus creates a plug firing sequencing as such: The first cylinder fires, the second (rear) cylinder fires 315° later, then there is a 405° gap until the first cylinder fires again, giving the engine its unique sound.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p><p>Harley-Davidson has used various ignition systems throughout its history – be it the early points and condenser system, (Big Twin up to 1978 and Sportsters up to 1978), magneto ignition system used on some 1958 to 1969 Sportsters, early electronic with centrifugal mechanical advance weights, (all models 1978 and a half to 1979), or the late electronic with transistorized ignition control module, more familiarly known as the black box or the brain, (all models 1980 to present).
</p><p>Starting in 1995, the company introduced Electronic Fuel Injection (EFI) as an option for the 30th anniversary edition <a href="/wiki/Electra_Glide" class="mw-redirect" title="Electra Glide">Electra Glide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-H-Dtimeline1990s_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H-Dtimeline1990s-112">[112]</a></sup> EFI became standard on all Harley-Davidson motorcycles, including Sportsters, upon the introduction of the 2007 product line.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>In 1991, Harley-Davidson began to participate in the Sound Quality Working Group, founded by Orfield Labs, Bruel and Kjaer, <a href="/wiki/TEAC_Corporation" title="TEAC Corporation">TEAC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yamaha" class="mw-redirect" title="Yamaha">Yamaha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sennheiser" title="Sennheiser">Sennheiser</a>, SMS and Cortex. This was the nation's first group to share research on psychological acoustics. Later that year, Harley-Davidson participated in a series of sound quality studies at Orfield Labs, based on recordings taken at the <a href="/wiki/Talladega_Superspeedway" title="Talladega Superspeedway">Talladega Superspeedway</a>, with the objective to lower the sound level for EU standards while analytically capturing the "Harley Sound".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This research resulted in the bikes that were introduced in compliance with EU standards for 1998.
</p><p>On February 1, 1994, the company filed a <a href="/wiki/Sound_trademark" title="Sound trademark">sound trademark</a> application for the distinctive sound of the Harley-Davidson motorcycle engine: "The mark consists of the exhaust sound of applicant's motorcycles, produced by V-twin, common crankpin motorcycle engines when the goods are in use". Nine of Harley-Davidson's competitors filed comments opposing the application, arguing that cruiser-style motorcycles of various brands use a single-crankpin V-twin engine which produce a similar sound.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> These objections were followed by litigation. In June 2000, the company dropped efforts to federally register its trademark.<sup id="cite_ref-ODell2000_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODell2000-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Popely_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Popely-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_V-twins">Big V-twins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Big V-twins" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/IOE_engine" title="IOE engine">F-head</a>, also known as JD, pocket valve and IOE (intake over exhaust), 1914–1929 (1,000 cc), and 1922–1929 (1,200 cc)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flathead_engine" title="Flathead engine">Flathead</a>, 1930–1949 (1,200 cc) and 1935–1941 (1,300 cc).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Knucklehead_engine" title="Harley-Davidson Knucklehead engine">Knucklehead</a>, 1936–1947 61 cubic inch (1,000 cc), and 1941–1947 74 cubic inch (1,200 cc)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Panhead_engine" title="Harley-Davidson Panhead engine">Panhead</a>, 1948–1965 61 cubic inch (1,000 cc), and 1948–1965, 74 cubic inch (1,200 cc)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Shovelhead_engine" title="Harley-Davidson Shovelhead engine">Shovelhead</a>, 1966–1984, 74 cubic inch (1,200 cc) and 80 cubic inch (1,338 cc) since late 1978</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Evolution_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Evolution engine">Evolution</a> (a.k.a. "Evo" and "Blockhead"), 1984–1999, 80 cubic inch (1,340 cc)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Twin_Cam_engine" title="Harley-Davidson Twin Cam engine">Twin Cam</a> (a.k.a. "Fathead" as named by American Iron Magazine) 1999–2017, in the following versions:
<ul><li>Twin Cam 88, 1999–2006, 88 cubic inch (1,450 cc)</li>
<li>Twin Cam 88B, counterbalanced version of the Twin Cam 88, 2000–2006, 88 cubic inch (1,450 cc)</li>
<li>Twin Cam 95, since 2000, 95 cubic inch (1,550 cc) (engines for early C.V.O. models)</li>
<li>Twin Cam 96, since 2007. As of 2012, only the Street Bob and Super Glide Custom Models still use the 96.96 cubic inch (1,584 cc)</li>
<li>Twin Cam 103, 2003–2006, 2009, 103 cubic inch (1,690 cc) (engines for C.V.O. models), Standard on 2011 Touring models: Ultra Limited, Road King Classic and Road Glide Ultra and optional on the Road Glide Custom and Street Glide. Standard on most 2012 models excluding Sportsters and 2 Dynas (Street Bob and Super Glide Custom). Standard on all 2014 dyna models.</li>
<li>Twin Cam 110, 2007–2017, 110 cubic inch (1,800 cc) (engines for C.V.O. models, 2016 Soft Tail Slim S; FatBoy S, Low Rider S, and Pro-Street Breakout)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Milwaukee-Eight_engines" class="mw-redirect" title="Harley-Davidson Milwaukee-Eight engines">Milwaukee-Eight</a>
