<ul><li>Twin-cooled 107 cu in (1,746 cc): Standard on touring and trike model year 2017+.<sup id="cite_ref-motorcycle.com_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-motorcycle.com-117">[117]</a></sup></li>
<li>Twin-cooled 114 cu in (1,868 cc): Optional on touring and trike model year 2017+, standard on 2017 CVO models.<sup id="cite_ref-motorcycle.com_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-motorcycle.com-117">[117]</a></sup></li>
<li>Twin-cooled 117 cu in (1,923 cc): Standard on 2018 CVO models<sup id="cite_ref-cvo_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cvo-118">[118]</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Small_V-twins">Small V-twins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Small V-twins" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sportster_moving.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Sportster_moving.jpg/220px-Sportster_moving.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Sportster_moving.jpg/220px-Sportster_moving.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sportster_moving.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Evolution Sportster</div></div></div>
<ul><li>D Model, 1929–1931, 750 cc</li>
<li>R Model, 1932–1936, 750 cc</li>
<li>W Model, 1937–1952, 750 cc, solo (2 wheel, frame only)</li>
<li>G (Servi-Car) Model, 1932–1973, 750 cc</li>
<li>K Model, 1952–1953, 750 cc</li>
<li>KH Model, 1954–1956, 900 cc</li>
<li>Ironhead, 1957–1971, 883 cc; 1972–1985, 1,000 cc</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Evolution_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Evolution engine">Evolution</a>, since 1986, 883 cc, 1,100 cc and 1,200 cc</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution_engine">Revolution engine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Revolution engine" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Motorcycle_engine_2012.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Motorcycle_engine_2012.jpg/220px-Motorcycle_engine_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4258" data-file-height="3368"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 174px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Motorcycle_engine_2012.jpg/220px-Motorcycle_engine_2012.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="174" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Motorcycle_engine_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Revolution engine in <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_VRSC" title="Harley-Davidson VRSC">V-Rod</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Revolution engine is based on the VR-1000 <a href="/wiki/Superbike" class="mw-redirect" title="Superbike">Superbike</a> race program, co-developed by Harley-Davidson's Powertrain Engineering team and <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> Engineering in <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>, Germany. It is a liquid cooled, dual overhead cam, internally counterbalanced 60 degree V-twin engine with a displacement of 69 cubic inch (1,130 cc), producing 115 hp (86 kW) at 8,250 rpm at the crank, with a redline of 9,000 rpm.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> It was introduced for the new <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_VRSC" title="Harley-Davidson VRSC">VRSC (V-Rod)</a> line in 2001 for the 2002 model year, starting with the single VRSCA (V-Twin Racing Street Custom) model.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The Revolution marks Harley's first collaboration with Porsche since the V4 Nova project, which, like the V-Rod, was a radical departure from Harley's traditional lineup until it was cancelled by AMF in 1981 in favor of the <a href="/wiki/Evolution_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Evolution engine">Evolution engine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Moy_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moy-123">[123]</a></sup></p><p>A 1,250 cc Screamin' Eagle version of the Revolution engine was made available for 2005 and 2006, and was present thereafter in a single production model from 2005 to 2007. In 2008, the 1,250 cc Revolution Engine became standard for the entire VRSC line. Harley-Davidson claims 123 hp (92 kW) at the crank for the 2008 VRSCAW model. The VRXSE <i>Destroyer</i> is equipped with a stroker (75 mm crank) Screamin' Eagle 79 cubic inch (1,300 cc) Revolution Engine, producing more than 165 hp (123 kW).
</p><p>750 cc and 500 cc versions of the Revolution engine are used in Harley-Davidson's <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Street" title="Harley-Davidson Street">Street line</a> of light cruisers.<sup id="cite_ref-popularmechanics_Street_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popularmechanics_Street-124">[124]</a></sup> These motors, named the Revolution X, use a single overhead cam, screw and locknut valve adjustment, a single internal counterbalancer, and vertically split crankcases; all of these changes making it different from the original Revolution design.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="D.C3.BCsseldorf-Test"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Düsseldorf-Test">Düsseldorf-Test</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Düsseldorf-Test" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>An extreme endurance test of the Revolution engine was performed in a dynometer installation, simulating the German <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a> (highways without general speed limit) between the Porsche research and development center in Weissach, near Stuttgart to <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>. Uncounted samples of engines failed, until an engine successfully passed the 500-hour nonstop run. This was the benchmark for the engineers to approve the start of production for the Revolution engine, which was documented in the <a href="/wiki/Discovery_channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Discovery channel">Discovery channel</a> special Harley-Davidson: Birth of the V-Rod, October 14, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-discovery_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-discovery-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Single-cylinder_engines">Single-cylinder engines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Single-cylinder engines" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_Davidson_1928_28B_1.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Harley_Davidson_1928_28B_1.jpg/220px-Harley_Davidson_1928_28B_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Harley_Davidson_1928_28B_1.jpg/220px-Harley_Davidson_1928_28B_1.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_Davidson_1928_28B_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1928 Harley-Davidson single-cylinder motorcycle</div></div></div>
<dl><dt>IOE singles</dt></dl><p>The first Harley-Davidson motorcycles were powered by <a href="/wiki/Single-cylinder_engine" title="Single-cylinder engine">single-cylinder</a> <a href="/wiki/IOE_engine" title="IOE engine">IOE engines</a> with the inlet valve operated by engine vacuum, based on the <a href="/wiki/De_Dion-Bouton" title="De Dion-Bouton">DeDion-Bouton</a> pattern.<sup id="cite_ref-GirdlerBreifHistory_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GirdlerBreifHistory-127">[127]</a></sup> Singles of this type continued to be made until 1913, when a pushrod and rocker system was used to operate the overhead inlet valve on the single, a similar system having been used on their V-twins since 1911.<sup id="cite_ref-ReffertyIlluDir44_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReffertyIlluDir44-128">[128]</a></sup> Single-cylinder motorcycle engines were discontinued in 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-GirdlerHDTimeline_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GirdlerHDTimeline-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<dl><dt>Flathead and OHV singles</dt></dl><p>Single-cylinder engines were reintroduced in 1925 as 1926 models.<sup id="cite_ref-HDCentury_1stFlathead_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDCentury_1stFlathead-130">[130]</a></sup> These singles were available either as <a href="/wiki/Flathead_engine" title="Flathead engine">flathead engines</a> or as <a href="/wiki/Overhead_valve" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhead valve">overhead valve</a> engines<sup id="cite_ref-CompleteHD32_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CompleteHD32-131">[131]</a></sup> until 1930, after which they were only available as flatheads.<sup id="cite_ref-HDCentury_1stFlathead_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDCentury_1stFlathead-130">[130]</a></sup> The flathead single-cylinder motorcycles were designated Model A for engines with magneto systems only and Model B for engines with battery and coil systems, while overhead valve versions were designated Model AA and Model BA respectively, and a magneto-only racing version was designated Model S.<sup id="cite_ref-CompleteHD32_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CompleteHD32-131">[131]</a></sup> This line of single-cylinder motorcycles ended production in 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-HDCentury_1stFlathead_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDCentury_1stFlathead-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<dl><dt>Two-stroke singles</dt></dl><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Hummer" title="Harley-Davidson Hummer">Harley-Davidson Hummer</a></div>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Model_families">Model families</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Model families" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>Modern Harley-branded motorcycles fall into one of six model families: Touring, Softail, Dyna, Sportster, Vrod and Street. These model families are distinguished by the frame, engine, suspension, and other characteristics.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Touring">Touring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Touring" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_FL" title="Harley-Davidson FL">Harley-Davidson FL</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PolizeiHarley.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/PolizeiHarley.JPG/220px-PolizeiHarley.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/PolizeiHarley.JPG/220px-PolizeiHarley.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PolizeiHarley.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hamburg Police <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_FL#Electra_Glide" title="Harley-Davidson FL">Electra Glide</a></div></div></div>
<p>Touring models use Big-Twin engines and large-diameter telescopic forks. All Touring designations begin with the letters FL, <i>e.g.</i>, FLHR (Road King) and FLTR (Road Glide).
</p><p>The touring family, also known as "dressers" or "baggers", includes Road King, Road Glide, Street Glide and Electra Glide models offered in various trims. The Road Kings have a "retro cruiser" appearance and are equipped with a large clear windshield. Road Kings are reminiscent of big-twin models from the 1940s and 1950s. Electra Glides can be identified by their full front fairings. Most Electra Glides sport a fork-mounted fairing referred to as the "Batwing" due to its unmistakable shape. The Road Glide and Road Glide Ultra Classic have a frame-mounted fairing, referred to as the "Sharknose". The Sharknose includes a unique, dual front headlight.
</p><p>Touring models are distinguishable by their large saddlebags, rear coil-over air suspension and are the only models to offer full fairings with radios and <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Band_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="Citizens Band radio">CBs</a>. All touring models use the same frame, first introduced with a Shovelhead motor in 1980, and carried forward with only modest upgrades until 2009, when it was extensively redesigned. The frame is distinguished by the location of the steering head in front of the forks and was the first H-D frame to rubber mount the drivetrain to isolate the rider from the vibration of the big V-twin.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley.electraglide.750pix.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Harley.electraglide.750pix.jpg/220px-Harley.electraglide.750pix.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="536"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 157px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Harley.electraglide.750pix.jpg/220px-Harley.electraglide.750pix.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="157" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley.electraglide.750pix.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Electra Glide "Ultra Classic"</div></div></div>
<p>The frame was modified for the 1993 model year when the oil tank went under the transmission and the battery was moved inboard from under the right saddlebag to under the seat. In 1997, the frame was again modified to allow for a larger battery under the seat and to lower seat height. In 2007, Harley-Davidson introduced the 96 cubic inches (1,570 cubic centimetres)<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Twin Cam 96 engine, as well the six-speed transmission to give the rider better speeds on the highway.
</p><p>In 2006, Harley introduced the FLHX Street Glide, a bike designed by Willie G. Davidson to be his personal ride, to its touring line.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p><p>In 2008, Harley added <a href="/wiki/Anti-lock_braking_system" title="Anti-lock braking system">anti-lock braking systems</a> and cruise control as a factory installed option on all touring models (standard on CVO and Anniversary models).<sup id="cite_ref-ABS_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABS-134">[134]</a></sup> Also new for 2008 is the 6-US-gallon (23 l; 5.0 imp gal) fuel tank for all touring models. 2008 also brought throttle-by-wire to all touring models.
</p><p>For the 2009 model year, Harley-Davidson redesigned the entire touring range with several changes, including a new frame, new swingarm, a completely revised engine-mounting system, 17-inch (430 mm) front wheels for all but the FLHRC Road King Classic, and a 2–1–2 exhaust. The changes result in greater load carrying capacity, better handling, a smoother engine, longer range and less exhaust heat transmitted to the rider and passenger.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
Also released for the 2009 model year is the FLHTCUTG Tri-Glide Ultra Classic, the first three-wheeled Harley since the Servi-Car was discontinued in 1973. The model features a unique frame and a 103-cubic-inch (1,690 cc) engine exclusive to the trike.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, Harley-Davidson released a redesign for specific touring bikes and called it "Project Rushmore".<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Changes include a new 103CI High Output engine, one handed easy open saddlebags and compartments, a new Boom! Box Infotainment system with either 4.3-inch (10 cm) or 6.5-inch (16.5 cm) screens featuring touchscreen functionality [6.5-inch (16.5 cm) models only], Bluetooth (media and phone with approved compatible devices), available GPS and SiriusXM, Text-to-Speech functionality (with approved compatible devices) and USB connectivity with charging. Other features include ABS with Reflex linked brakes, improved styling, Halogen or LED lighting and upgraded passenger comfort.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Softail">Softail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Softail" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Softail" title="Softail">Softail</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Evb-my_hog.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Evb-my_hog.jpg/220px-Evb-my_hog.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Evb-my_hog.jpg/220px-Evb-my_hog.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Evb-my_hog.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2002 <a href="/wiki/Softail" title="Softail">Softail</a> Heritage Classic</div></div></div>
<p>These big-twin motorcycles capitalize on Harley's strong value on tradition. With the rear-wheel suspension hidden under the transmission, they are visually similar to the "hardtail" <a href="/wiki/Chopper_(motorcycle)" title="Chopper (motorcycle)">choppers</a> popular in the 1960s and 1970s, as well as from their own earlier history. In keeping with that tradition, Harley offers Softail models with "Heritage" styling that incorporate design cues from throughout their history and used to offer "Springer" front ends on these Softail models from the factory.
</p>
<dl><dt>Designation</dt></dl><p>Softail models utilize the big-twin engine (F) and the Softail chassis (ST).
</p>
<ul><li>Softail models that use 21-inch (530 mm) Front Wheels have designations that begin with FX, <i>e.g.</i>, FXSTB (Night Train), FXSTD (Deuce), and FXSTS (Springer).</li>
<li>Softail models that use 16-inch (410 mm) Front Wheels have designations beginning with FL, <i>e.g.</i>, FLSTF (Fat Boy), FLSTC (Heritage Softail Classic), FLSTN (Softail Deluxe) and FLS (Softail Slim).</li>
<li>Softail models that use Springer forks with a 21-inch (530 mm) wheel have designations that begin with FXSTS, <i>e.g.</i>, FXSTS (Springer Softail) and FXSTSB (Bad Boy).</li>
<li>Softail models that use Springer forks with a 16-inch (410 mm) wheel have designations that begin with FLSTS, <i>e.g.</i>, FLSTSC (Springer Classic) and FLSTSB (Cross Bones).</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Dyna">Dyna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Dyna" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Super_Glide" title="Harley-Davidson Super Glide">Harley-Davidson Super Glide</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_18.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Harley-Davidson_18.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_18.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Harley-Davidson_18.jpg/220px-Harley-Davidson_18.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley-Davidson_18.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2005 Dyna <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Super_Glide" title="Harley-Davidson Super Glide">Super Glide</a> Custom.</div></div></div>
<p>Dyna-frame motorcycles were developed in the 1980s and early 1990s and debuted in the 1991 model year with the FXDB Sturgis offered in limited edition quantities. In 1992 the line continued with the limited edition FXDB Daytona and a production model FXD Super Glide. The new DYNA frame featured big-twin engines and traditional styling. They can be distinguished from the Softail by the traditional coil-over suspension that connects the swingarm to the frame, and from the Sportster by their larger engines. On these models, the transmission also houses the engine's oil reservoir.
</p><p>Prior to 2006, Dyna models typically featured a narrow, XL-style 39mm front fork and front wheel, as well as footpegs which the manufacturer included the letter "X" in the model designation to indicate. This lineup traditionally included the Super Glide (FXD), Super Glide Custom (FXDC), Street Bob (FXDB), and Low Rider (FXDL). One exception was the Wide Glide (FXDWG), which featured thicker 41mm forks and a narrow front wheel, but positioned the forks on wider triple-trees that give a beefier appearance. In 2008, the Dyna Fat Bob (FXDF) was introduced to the Dyna lineup, featuring aggressive styling like a new 2–1–2 exhaust, twin headlamps, a 180 mm rear tire, and, for the first time in the Dyna lineup, a 130 mm front tire. For the 2012 model year, the Dyna Switchback (FLD) became the first Dyna to break the tradition of having an FX model designation with floorboards, detachable painted hard saddlebags, touring windshield, headlight nacelle and a wide front tire with full fender.  The new front end resembled the big-twin FL models from 1968 to 1971.
</p><p>The Dyna family used the 88-cubic-inch (1,440 cc) twin cam from 1999 to 2006. In 2007, the displacement was increased to 96 cubic inches (1,570 cc) as the factory increased the stroke to 4.375 inches (111.1 mm). For the 2012 model year, the manufacturer began to offer Dyna models with the 103-cubic-inch (1,690 cc) upgrade.  All Dyna models use a rubber-mounted engine to isolate engine vibration. Harley discontinued the Dyna platform in 2017 for the 2018 model year, having been replaced by a completely-redesigned <a href="/wiki/Softail" title="Softail">Softail</a> chassis; some of the existing models previously released by the company under the Dyna nameplate have since been carried over to the new Softail line.<sup id="cite_ref-firstlooks_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstlooks-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<dl><dt>Designation</dt></dl><p>Dyna models utilize the big-twin engine (F), footpegs noted as (X) with the exception of the 2012 FLD Switchback, a Dyna model which used floorboards as featured on the Touring (L) models, and the Dyna chassis (D). Therefore, except for the FLD from 2012 to 2016, all Dyna models have designations that begin with FXD, <i>e.g.</i>, FXDWG (Dyna Wide Glide) and FXDL (Dyna Low Rider).
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sportster">Sportster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sportster" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Sportster" title="Harley-Davidson Sportster">Harley-Davidson Sportster</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:200501DIRTYDEBBIE_003a.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/200501DIRTYDEBBIE_003a.jpg/220px-200501DIRTYDEBBIE_003a.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="577" data-file-height="410"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 156px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/200501DIRTYDEBBIE_003a.jpg/220px-200501DIRTYDEBBIE_003a.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="156" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:200501DIRTYDEBBIE_003a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2002 <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Sportster" title="Harley-Davidson Sportster">Sportster</a> 883 Custom</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2003_HD_XL1200C_Anniversary_Edition.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/2003_HD_XL1200C_Anniversary_Edition.jpg/220px-2003_HD_XL1200C_Anniversary_Edition.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/2003_HD_XL1200C_Anniversary_Edition.jpg/220px-2003_HD_XL1200C_Anniversary_Edition.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2003_HD_XL1200C_Anniversary_Edition.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2003 Harley-Davidson XL1200 Custom Anniversary Edition</div></div></div>
<p>Introduced in 1957, the Sportster family were conceived as racing motorcycles, and were popular on dirt and flat-track race courses through the 1960s and 1970s. Smaller and lighter than the other Harley models, contemporary Sportsters make use of 883 cc or 1,200 cc Evolution engines and, though often modified, remain similar in appearance to their racing ancestors.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p><p>Up until the 2003 model year, the engine on the Sportster was rigidly mounted to the frame. The 2004 Sportster received a new frame accommodating a rubber-mounted engine. This made the bike heavier and reduced the available lean angle, while it reduced the amount of vibration transmitted to the frame and the rider, providing a smoother ride for rider and passenger.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p><p>In the 2007 model year, Harley-Davidson celebrated the 50th anniversary of the Sportster and produced a limited edition called the XL50, of which only 2000 were made for sale worldwide. Each motorcycle was individually numbered and came in one of two colors, Mirage Pearl Orange or Vivid Black. Also in 2007, electronic fuel injection was introduced to the Sportster family, and the Nightster model was introduced in mid-year. In 2009, Harley-Davidson added the Iron 883 to the Sportster line, as part of the Dark Custom series.
In the 2008 model year, Harley-Davidson released the XR1200 Sportster in Europe, Africa, and the Middle East. The XR1200 had an Evolution engine tuned to produce 91 bhp (68 kW), four-piston dual front disc brakes, and an aluminum swing arm.  <i><a href="/wiki/Motorcyclist_(magazine)" title="Motorcyclist (magazine)">Motorcyclist</a></i> featured the XR1200 on the cover of its July 2008 issue and was generally positive about it in their "First Ride" story, in which Harley-Davidson was repeatedly asked to sell it in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
One possible reason for the delayed availability in the United States was the fact that Harley-Davidson had to obtain the "XR1200" naming rights from Storz Performance, a Harley customizing shop in Ventura, Calif.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The XR1200 was released in the United States in 2009 in a special color scheme including Mirage Orange highlighting its dirt-tracker heritage. The first 750 XR1200 models in 2009 were pre-ordered and came with a number 1 tag for the front of the bike, autographed by <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Coolbeth" title="Kenny Coolbeth">Kenny Coolbeth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Parker_(motorcyclist)" title="Scott Parker (motorcyclist)">Scott Parker</a> and a thank you/welcome letter from the company, signed by Bill Davidson.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The XR1200 was discontinued in model year 2013.
</p>
<dl><dt>Designation</dt></dl><p>Except for the street-going XR1000 of the 1980s and the XR1200, most Sportsters made for street use have the prefix XL in their model designation. For the Sportster Evolution engines used since the mid-1980s, there have been two engine sizes. Motorcycles with the smaller engine are designated XL883, while those with the larger engine were initially designated XL1100. When the size of the larger engine was increased from 1,100 cc to 1,200 cc, the designation was changed accordingly from XL1100 to XL1200. Subsequent letters in the designation refer to model variations within the Sportster range, e.g. the XL883C refers to an 883 cc Sportster Custom, while the XL1200S designates the now-discontinued 1200 Sportster Sport.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="VRSC">VRSC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: VRSC" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_VRSC" title="Harley-Davidson VRSC">Harley-Davidson VRSC</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_5-06.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/Harley_5-06.jpg/220px-Harley_5-06.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/Harley_5-06.jpg/220px-Harley_5-06.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_5-06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2003 VRSCA V-Rod</div></div></div>
<p>Introduced in 2001 and produced until 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-last_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-last-144">[144]</a></sup> the VRSC muscle bike family bears little resemblance to Harley's more traditional lineup. Competing against Japanese and American muscle bikes in the upcoming <a href="/wiki/Power_cruiser" class="mw-redirect" title="Power cruiser">muscle bike/power cruiser</a> segment, the "V-Rod" makes use of an engine developed jointly with <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> that, for the first time in Harley history, incorporates <a href="/wiki/Overhead_cam" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhead cam">overhead cams</a> and liquid cooling. The V-Rod is visually distinctive, easily identified by the 60-degree V-Twin engine, the radiator and the <a href="/wiki/Hydroforming" title="Hydroforming">hydroformed</a> frame members that support the round-topped air cleaner cover. The VRSC <a href="/wiki/Automobile_platform" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile platform">platform</a> was also used for factory drag-racing motorcycles.
</p><p>In 2008, Harley added the anti-lock braking system as a factory installed option on all VRSC models.<sup id="cite_ref-ABS_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABS-134">[134]</a></sup> Harley also increased the displacement of the stock engine from 1,130 to 1,250 cc (69 to 76 cu in), which had only previously been available from Screamin' Eagle, and added a slipper clutch as standard equipment.
</p><p>VRSC models include:
</p>
<ul><li>VRSCA: V-Rod (2002–2006), VRSCAW: V-Rod (2007–2010), VRSCB: V-Rod (2004–2005), VRSCD: Night Rod (2006–2008), VRSCDX: Night Rod Special (2007–2014), VRSCSE: Screamin' Eagle CVO V-Rod (2005), VRSCSE2: Screamin' Eagle CVO V-Rod (2006), VRSCR: Street Rod (2006–2007), VRSCX: Screamin' Eagle Tribute V-Rod (2007), VRSCF: V-Rod Muscle (2009–2014).</li></ul><dl><dt>Designation</dt></dl><p>VRSC models utilize the Revolution engine (VR), and the street versions are designated Street Custom (SC). After the VRSC prefix common to all street Revolution bikes, the next letter denotes the model, either A (base V-Rod: discontinued), AW (base V-Rod + W for Wide with a 240 mm rear tire), B (discontinued), D (Night Rod: discontinued), R (Street Rod: discontinued), SE and SEII(CVO Special Edition), or X (Special edition). Further differentiation within models are made with an additional letter, <i>e.g.</i>, VRSCDX denotes the Night Rod Special.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="VRXSE">VRXSE</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: VRXSE" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>The VRXSE V-Rod Destroyer is Harley-Davidson's production drag racing motorcycle, constructed to run the quarter mile in less than ten seconds. It is based on the same revolution engine that powers the VRSC line, but the VRXSE uses the Screamin' Eagle 1,300 cc "stroked" incarnation, featuring a 75 mm crankshaft, 105 mm Pistons, and 58 mm throttle bodies.
</p><p>The V-Rod Destroyer is not a street legal motorcycle. As such, it uses "X" instead of "SC" to denote a non-street bike.  "SE" denotes a CVO Special Edition.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Street">Street</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Street" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Street" title="Harley-Davidson Street">Harley-Davidson Street</a></div>
<p>The Street, Harley-Davidson's newest platform and their first all new platform in thirteen years, was designed to appeal to younger riders looking for a lighter bike at a cheaper price.<sup id="cite_ref-popularmechanics_Street_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popularmechanics_Street-124">[124]</a></sup> The Street 750 model was launched in India at the 2014 Indian Auto Expo, Delhi-NCR on February 5, 2014. The Street 750 weighs 218 kg and has a ground clearance of 144 mm giving it the lowest weight and the highest ground clearance of Harley-Davidson motorcycles currently available.<sup id="cite_ref-Zig20140205_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zig20140205-145">[145]</a></sup></p><p>The Street 750 uses an all-new, liquid-cooled, 60° V-twin engine called the Revolution X. In the Street 750, the engine displaces 749 cc (45.7 cu in) and produces 65 Nm at 4,000 rpm. A six speed transmission is used.<sup id="cite_ref-Zig20140205_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zig20140205-145">[145]</a></sup></p><p>The Street 750 and the smaller-displacement Street 500 has been available since late 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-popularmechanics_Street_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popularmechanics_Street-124">[124]</a></sup> Street series motorcycles for the North American market will be built in Harley-Davidson's Kansas City, Missouri plant,<sup id="cite_ref-popularmechanics_Street_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popularmechanics_Street-124">[124]</a></sup> while those for other markets around the world will be built completely in their plant in Bawal, India.<sup id="cite_ref-popularmechanics_Street_124-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popularmechanics_Street-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zig20140205_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zig20140205-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Custom_Vehicle_Operations">Custom Vehicle Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Custom Vehicle Operations" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_CVO" title="Harley-Davidson CVO">Harley-Davidson CVO</a></div>
<p>Custom Vehicle Operations (CVO) is a team within Harley-Davidson that produces limited-edition customizations of Harley's stock models. Every year since 1999, the team has selected two to five of the company's base models and added higher-displacement engines, performance upgrades, special-edition paint jobs, more chromed or accented components, audio system upgrades, and electronic accessories to create high-dollar, premium-quality customizations for the <a href="/wiki/Custom_motorcycle" title="Custom motorcycle">factory custom</a> market.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The models most commonly upgraded in such a fashion are the Ultra Classic Electra Glide, which has been selected for CVO treatment every year from 2006 to the present, and the Road King, which was selected in 2002, 2003, 2007, and 2008. The Dyna, Softail, and VRSC families have also been selected for CVO customization.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Environmental record" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a> conducted emissions-certification and representative emissions test in <a href="/wiki/Ann_Arbor,_Michigan" title="Ann Arbor, Michigan">Ann Arbor, Michigan</a>, in 2005. Subsequently, Harley-Davidson produced an "environmental warranty". The warranty ensures each owner that the vehicle is designed and built free of any defects in materials and workmanship that would cause the vehicle to not meet EPA standards.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> In 2005, the EPA and the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Department_of_Environmental_Protection" title="Pennsylvania Department of Environmental Protection">Pennsylvania Department of Environmental Protection</a> (PADEP) confirmed Harley-Davidson to be the first corporation to voluntarily enroll in the One Clean-Up Program. This program is designed for the clean-up of the affected soil and groundwater at the former York Naval Ordnance Plant. The program is backed by the state and local government along with participating organizations and corporations.<sup id="cite_ref-vupxae_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vupxae-148">[148]</a></sup></p><p>Paul Gotthold, Director of Operations for the EPA, congratulated the motor company:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Harley-Davidson has taken their environmental responsibilities very seriously and has already made substantial progress in the investigation and cleanup of past contamination. Proof of Harley's efforts can be found in the recent EPA determination that designates the Harley property as 'under control' for cleanup purposes. This determination means that there are no serious contamination problems at the facility. Under the new One Cleanup Program, Harley, EPA, and PADEP will expedite the completion of the property investigation and reach a final solution that will permanently protect human health and the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-vupxae_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vupxae-148">[148]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Harley-Davidson also purchased most of Castalloy, a South Australian producer of cast motorcycle wheels and hubs. The South Australian government has set forth "protection to the purchaser (Harley-Davidson) against environmental risks".<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2016 Harley-Davidson settled with the EPA for $12 million, without admitting wrongdoing, over the sale of <a href="/wiki/Aftermarket_(automotive)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aftermarket (automotive)">after-market</a> "super tuners".<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Super tuners were devices, marketed for competition, which enabled increased performance of Harley-Davidson products. However, the devices also modified the emission control systems, producing increased <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxide</a>. Harley-Davidson is required to buy back and destroy any super tuners which do not meet <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act</a> requirements and spend $3 million on air pollution mitigation.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Sponsorship" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Bucks" title="Milwaukee Bucks">Milwaukee Bucks</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> sport a Harley Davidson sponsor patch on their jerseys.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_culture">Brand culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Brand culture" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarleyDavidsonCafeLV.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/HarleyDavidsonCafeLV.jpg/220px-HarleyDavidsonCafeLV.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/HarleyDavidsonCafeLV.jpg/220px-HarleyDavidsonCafeLV.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HarleyDavidsonCafeLV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harley-Davidson Cafe <a href="/wiki/Theme_restaurant" title="Theme restaurant">theme restaurant</a> located on the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip" title="Las Vegas Strip">Las Vegas Strip</a></div></div></div>
<p>According to a recent Harley-Davidson study, in 1987 half of all Harley riders were under age 35.<sup id="cite_ref-age35_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age35-152">[152]</a></sup> Now, only 15 percent of Harley buyers are under 35,<sup id="cite_ref-age35_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age35-152">[152]</a></sup> and as of 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> age had risen to 46.7.<sup id="cite_ref-age46.7_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age46.7-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-age47_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age47-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-seniors_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seniors-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chart_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chart-156">[156]</a></sup> In 2008, Harley-Davidson stopped disclosing the average age of riders; at this point it was 48 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p><p>In 1987, the <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> household income of a Harley-Davidson rider was $38,000. By 1997, the <a href="/wiki/Median_household_income" class="mw-redirect" title="Median household income">median household income</a> for those riders had more than doubled, to $83,000.<sup id="cite_ref-age35-2_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-age35-2-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2009)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Many Harley-Davidson Clubs exist nowadays around the world;<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> the oldest one, founded in 1928, is in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p><p>Harley-Davidson attracts a loyal <a href="/wiki/Brand_community" title="Brand community">brand community</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> with licensing of the Harley-Davidson logo accounting for almost 5 percent of the company's net revenue ($41 million in 2004).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> Harley-Davidson supplies many American police forces with their motorcycle fleets.<sup id="cite_ref-On_Patrol_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-On_Patrol-163">[163]</a></sup></p><p>From its founding, Harley-Davidson had worked to brand its motorcycles as respectable and refined products, with ads that showed what motorcycling writer Fred Rau called "refined-looking ladies with parasols, and men in conservative suits as the target market".<sup id="cite_ref-Rau2007_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rau2007-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rau2008_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rau2008-165">[165]</a></sup> The 1906 Harley-Davidson's effective, and polite, muffler was emphasized in advertisements with the nickname <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Model_7D" title="Harley-Davidson Model 7D">"The Silent Gray Fellow"</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rau2008_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rau2008-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hook2002_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hook2002-166">[166]</a></sup> That began to shift in the 1960s, partially in response to the clean-cut motorcyclist portrayed in Honda's "<a href="/wiki/You_meet_the_nicest_people_on_a_Honda" class="mw-redirect" title="You meet the nicest people on a Honda">You meet the nicest people on a Honda</a>" campaign, when Harley-Davidson sought to draw a contrast with Honda by underscoring the more working-class, macho, and even a little anti-social attitude associated with motorcycling's dark side. With the 1971 <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Super_Glide" title="Harley-Davidson Super Glide">FX Super Glide</a>, the company embraced, rather than distanced, itself from <a href="/wiki/Chopper_(motorcycle)" title="Chopper (motorcycle)">chopper</a> style, and the counterculture custom Harley scene.<sup id="cite_ref-100_Years_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100_Years-167">[167]</a></sup> Their marketing cultivated the "bad boy" image of <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle#Social_aspects" title="Motorcycle">biker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_club" title="Motorcycle club">motorcycle clubs</a>, and to a point, even <a href="/wiki/Outlaw_motorcycle_club" title="Outlaw motorcycle club">outlaw or one-percenter</a> motorcycle clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-Rau2007_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rau2007-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rau2008_165-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rau2008-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Origin_of_.22Hog.22_nickname"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='Origin_of_"Hog"_nickname'>Origin of "Hog" nickname</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title='Edit section: Origin of "Hog" nickname' data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Beginning in 1920, a team of farm boys, including <a href="/wiki/Ray_Weishaar" title="Ray Weishaar">Ray Weishaar</a>, who became known as the "hog boys", consistently won races. The group had a live <a href="/wiki/Hog_(swine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hog (swine)">hog</a> as their <a href="/wiki/Mascot" title="Mascot">mascot</a>. Following a win, they would put the hog on their Harley and take a <a href="/wiki/Victory_lap" title="Victory lap">victory lap</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-H-Dtimeline1920s_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H-Dtimeline1920s-168">[168]</a></sup> In 1983, the Motor Company formed a club for owners of its product, taking advantage of the long-standing nickname by turning "hog" into the acronym HOG, for Harley Owners Group. Harley-Davidson attempted to trademark "hog", but lost a case against an independent Harley-Davidson specialist, The Hog Farm of West Seneca, New York,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> in 1999, when the <a href="/wiki/Appeal" title="Appeal">appellate panel</a> ruled that "hog" had become a <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/generic" class="extiw" title="wikt:generic">generic term</a> for large motorcycles and was therefore unprotectable as a trademark.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p><p>On August 15, 2006, Harley-Davidson Inc. had its NYSE ticker symbol changed from HDI to HOG.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Bobbers">Bobbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Bobbers" data-section="39" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Harley-Davidson FL "big twins" normally had heavy steel fenders, chrome trim, and other ornate and heavy accessories. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, riders wanting more speed would often shorten the fenders or take them off completely to reduce the weight of the motorcycle. These bikes were called "bobbers" or sometimes "choppers", because parts considered unnecessary were chopped off. Those who made or rode choppers and bobbers, especially members of motorcycle clubs like the <a href="/wiki/Hells_Angels" title="Hells Angels">Hells Angels</a>, referred to stock FLs as "garbage wagons".<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Harley_Owners_Group">Harley Owners Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Harley Owners Group" data-section="40" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harley_Owners_Group" title="Harley Owners Group">Harley Owners Group</a></div>
<p>Harley-Davidson established the <a href="/wiki/Harley_Owners_Group" title="Harley Owners Group">Harley Owners Group</a> (HOG) in 1983 to build on the loyalty of Harley-Davidson enthusiasts as a means to promote a lifestyle alongside its products. The HOG also opened new revenue streams for the company, with the production of tie-in merchandise offered to club members, numbering more than one million. Other motorcycle brands,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
and other and consumer brands outside motorcycling, have also tried to create factory-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Community_marketing" title="Community marketing">community marketing</a> clubs of their own.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup>
HOG members typically spend 30 percent more than other Harley owners on such items as clothing and Harley-Davidson-sponsored events.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p><p>In 1991, HOG went international, with the first official European HOG Rally in Cheltenham, England.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup>
Today, more than one million members and more than 1400 chapters worldwide make HOG the largest factory-sponsored motorcycle organization in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p><p>HOG benefits include organized group rides, exclusive products and product discounts, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.insurance.harley-davidson.com/">insurance discounts</a>, and the Hog Tales newsletter. A one-year full membership is included with the purchase of a new, unregistered Harley-Davidson.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p><p>In 2008, HOG celebrated its 25th anniversary in conjunction with the Harley 105th in Milwaukee, Wisconsin.
</p><p>3rd Southern HOG Rally set to bring together largest gathering of Harley-Davidson owners in South India. More than 600 Harley-Davidson Owners expected to ride to Hyderabad from across 13 HOG Chapters<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Factory_tours_and_museum">Factory tours and museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Factory tours and museum" data-section="41" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:35%;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:HD_museum_panorama.jpg" class="image" title="Harley-Davidson Museum in Milwaukee"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/HD_museum_panorama.jpg/1000px-HD_museum_panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="195" data-file-width="8565" data-file-height="1671"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 1000px;height: 195px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/HD_museum_panorama.jpg/1000px-HD_museum_panorama.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="1000" data-height="195"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HD_museum_panorama.jpg" title="File:HD museum panorama.jpg"> </a></div>Harley-Davidson Museum in Milwaukee</div></div></div>
<p>Harley-Davidson offers factory tours at four of its manufacturing sites, and the <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson_Museum" title="Harley-Davidson Museum">Harley-Davidson Museum</a>, which opened in 2008, exhibits Harley-Davidson's history, culture, and vehicles, including the motor company's corporate archives.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/York,_Pennsylvania" title="York, Pennsylvania">York, Pennsylvania</a> – Vehicle Operations: Manufacturing site for Touring class, Softail, and custom vehicles.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tomahawk,_Wisconsin" title="Tomahawk, Wisconsin">Tomahawk, Wisconsin</a> – Tomahawk Operations: Facility that makes sidecars, saddlebags, windshields, and more.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri" title="Kansas City, Missouri">Kansas City, Missouri</a> – Vehicle and Powertrain Operations: Manufacturing site of Sportster, VRSC, and other vehicles.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Menomonee_Falls,_Wisconsin" title="Menomonee Falls, Wisconsin">Menomonee Falls, Wisconsin</a> – Pilgrim Road Powertrain Operations plant, two types of tours.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee, Wisconsin</a> – Harley-Davidson Museum: Archive; exhibits of people, products, culture and history; restaurant &amp; café; and museum store.</li></ul><p>Due to the consolidation of operations, the Capitol Drive Tour Center in <a href="/wiki/Wauwatosa,_Wisconsin" title="Wauwatosa, Wisconsin">Wauwatosa, Wisconsin</a>, was closed in 2009.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Anniversary_celebrations">Anniversary celebrations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Anniversary celebrations" data-section="42" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_Davidson_founders.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Harley_Davidson_founders.jpg/170px-Harley_Davidson_founders.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="220" data-file-height="286"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 221px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Harley_Davidson_founders.jpg/170px-Harley_Davidson_founders.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="221" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley_Davidson_founders.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clockwise from top left: William S. Harley, William A. Davidson, Walter Davidson, Sr., Arthur Davidson</div></div></div>
<p>Beginning with Harley-Davidson's 90th anniversary in 1993, Harley-Davidson has had celebratory rides to <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a> called the "Ride Home".<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> This new tradition has continued every five years, and is referred to unofficially as "Harleyfest", in line with Milwaukee's other festivals (Summerfest, German fest, Festa Italiana, etc.). This event brings Harley riders from all around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> The 105th anniversary celebration was held on August 28–31, 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> and included events in Milwaukee, Waukesha, Racine, and Kenosha counties, in Southeast Wisconsin. The 110th anniversary celebration was held on August 29–31, 2013. The 115th anniversary was held in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, the home country of the oldest existing Harley Davidson Club, on July 5–8, 2018 and attracted more than 100.000 visitors and 60.000 bikes.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_Hall_of_Fame">Labor Hall of Fame</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Labor Hall of Fame" data-section="43" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>William S. Harley, Arthur Davidson, William A. Davidson and Walter Davidson, Sr were, in 2004, inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Labor_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor Hall of Fame">Labor Hall of Fame</a> for their accomplishments for the H-D company and its workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_drama">Television drama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harley-Davidson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Television drama" data-section="44" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company's origins were dramatized in a 2016 miniseries entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Harley_and_the_Davidsons" title="Harley and the Davidsons">Harley and the Davidsons</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Robert_Aramayo" title="Robert Aramayo">Robert Aramayo</a> as William Harley, <a href="/wiki/Bug_Hall" title="Bug Hall">Bug Hall</a> as Arthur Davidson<sup id="cite_ref-Walsh_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walsh-188">[188]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Michiel_Huisman" title="Michiel Huisman">Michiel Huisman</a> as Walter Davidson, and premiered on the <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Channel" title="Discovery Channel">Discovery Channel</a> as a "three-night event series" on September 5, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-dscHarley_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dscHarley-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ryan_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ryan-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Harley-Davidson Museum, Milwaukee, Wisconsin, various artifacts, ephemera, and placards. One placard states "<i>Harley-Davidson began as a motorcycle manufacturer unlike competitors such as Indian and Pope, which has [</i>sic<i>] previous histories in bicycling prior to building motorcycles. The many connections between bicycling and motorcycling prompted Harley-Davidson to begin selling bicycles in 1917. Despite heavy promotion, sales were disappointing and production was discontinued in 1923.</i>"</span>
